Callers can also\n172:   /// pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\n173:   LLVM_ABI void registerFunctionAnalyses(FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM);\n174: \n175:   /// Registers all available loop analysis passes.\n176:   ///\n177:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\c LoopAnalysisManager\n178:   /// with all registered loop analyses. Callers can still manually register any\n179:   /// additional analyses.\n180:   LLVM_ABI void registerLoopAnalyses(LoopAnalysisManager &LAM);\n181: \n182:   /// Registers all available machine function analysis passes.\n183:   ///\n184:   /// This is an interface that can be used to populate a \\c\n185:   /// MachineFunctionAnalysisManager with all registered function analyses.\n186:   /// Callers can still manually register any additional analyses. Callers can\n187:   /// also pre-register analyses and this will not override those.\n188:   LLVM_ABI void\n189:   registerMachineFunctionAnalyses(MachineFunctionAnalysisManager &MFAM);\n190: \n191:   /// Construct the core LLVM function canonicalization and simplification\n192:   /// pipeline.\n193:   ///\n194:   /// This is a long pipeline and uses most of the per-function optimization\n195:   /// passes in LLVM to canonicalize and simplify the IR. It is suitable to run\n196:   /// repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy important\n197:   /// information about the semantics of the IR.\n198:   ///\n199:   /// Note that \\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\n200:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\n201:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\n202:   /// build them.\n203:   ///\n204:   /// \\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\n205:   LLVM_ABI FunctionPassManager buildFunctionSimplificationPipeline(\n206:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n207: \n208:   /// Construct the core LLVM module canonicalization and simplification\n209:   /// pipeline.\n210:   ///\n211:   /// This pipeline focuses on canonicalizing and simplifying the entire module\n212:   /// of IR. Much like the function simplification pipeline above, it is\n213:   /// suitable to run repeatedly over the IR and is not expected to destroy\n214:   /// important information. It does, however, perform inlining and other\n215:   /// heuristic based simplifications that are not strictly reversible.\n216:   ///\n217:   /// Note that \\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\n218:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\n219:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\n220:   /// build them.\n221:   ///\n222:   /// \\p Phase indicates the current ThinLTO phase.\n223:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleSimplificationPipeline(\n224:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n225: \n226:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining as well as\n227:   /// the inlining-driven cleanups.\n228:   LLVM_ABI ModuleInlinerWrapperPass\n229:   buildInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n230: \n231:   /// Construct the module pipeline that performs inlining with\n232:   /// module inliner pass.\n233:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager\n234:   buildModuleInlinerPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n235: \n236:   /// Construct the core LLVM module optimization pipeline.\n237:   ///\n238:   /// This pipeline focuses on optimizing the execution speed of the IR. It\n239:   /// uses cost modeling and thresholds to balance code growth against runtime\n240:   /// improvements. It includes vectorization and other information destroying\n241:   /// transformations. It also cannot generally be run repeatedly on a module\n242:   /// without potentially seriously regressing either runtime performance of\n243:   /// the code or serious code size growth.\n244:   ///\n245:   /// Note that \\p Level cannot be `O0` here. The pipelines produced are\n246:   /// only intended for use when attempting to optimize code. If frontends\n247:   /// require some transformations for semantic reasons, they should explicitly\n248:   /// build them.\n249:   LLVM_ABI ModulePassManager buildModuleOptimizationPipeline(\n250:       OptimizationLevel Level, ThinOrFullLTOPhase LTOPhase);\n251: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h%3FL100-250"}}}

            bool CallHasNoUnwindAttr) {\n913:   if (Args.empty())\n914:     return {};\n915: \n916:   // To address unwind, the function should have nounwind attribute or the\n917:   // arguments have dead or invisible on unwind. Otherwise, return empty.\n918:   for (const auto &Arg : Args) {\n919:     if (!CallHasNoUnwindAttr && !Arg.IsDeadOrInvisibleOnUnwind)\n920:       return {};\n921:     if (Arg.Inits.empty())\n922:       return {};\n923:   }\n924: \n925:   ConstantRangeList IntersectedIntervals = Args.front().Inits;\n926:   for (auto &Arg : Args.drop_front())\n927:     IntersectedIntervals = IntersectedIntervals.intersectWith(Arg.Inits);\n928: \n929:   return IntersectedIntervals;\n930: }\n931: \n932: namespace {\n933: \n934: struct DSEState {\n935:   Function &F;\n936:   AliasAnalysis &AA;\n937:   EarliestEscapeAnalysis EA;\n938: \n939:   /// The single BatchAA instance that is used to cache AA queries. It will\n940:   /// not be invalidated over the whole run. This is safe, because:\n941:   /// 1. Only memory writes are removed, so the alias cache for memory\n942:   ///    locations remains valid.\n943:   /// 2. No new instructions are added (only instructions removed), so cached\n944:   ///    information for a deleted value cannot be accessed by a re-used new\n945:   ///    value pointer.\n946:   BatchAAResults BatchAA;\n947: \n948:   MemorySSA &MSSA;\n949:   DominatorTree &DT;\n950:   PostDominatorTree &PDT;\n951:   const TargetLibraryInfo &TLI;\n952:   const DataLayout &DL;\n953:   const LoopInfo &LI;\n954: \n955:   // Whether the function contains any irreducible control flow, useful for\n956:   // being accurately able to detect loops.\n957:   bool ContainsIrreducibleLoops;\n958: \n959:   // All MemoryDefs that potentially could kill other MemDefs.\n960:   SmallVector<MemoryDef *, 64> MemDefs;\n961:   // Any that should be skipped as they are already deleted\n962:   SmallPtrSet<MemoryAccess *, 4> SkipStores;\n963:   // Keep track whether a given object is captured before return or not.\n964:   DenseMap<const Value *, bool> CapturedBeforeReturn;\n965:   // Keep track of all of the objects that are invisible to the caller after\n966:   // the function returns.\n967:   DenseMap<const Value *, bool> InvisibleToCallerAfterRet;\n968:   DenseMap<const Value *, uint64_t> InvisibleToCallerAfterRetBounded;\n969:   // Keep track of blocks with throwing instructions not modeled in MemorySSA.\n970:   SmallPtrSet<BasicBlock *, 16> ThrowingBlocks;\n971:   // Post-order numbers for each basic block. Used to figure out if memory\n972:   // accesses are executed before another access.\n973:   DenseMap<BasicBlock *, unsigned> PostOrderNumbers;\n974: \n975:   /// Keep track of instructions (partly) overlapping with killing MemoryDefs per\n976:   /// basic block.\n977:   MapVector<BasicBlock *, InstOverlapIntervalsTy> IOLs;\n978:   // Check if there are root nodes that are terminated by UnreachableInst.\n979:   // Those roots pessimize post-dominance queries. If there are such roots,\n980:   // fall back to CFG scan starting from all non-unreachable roots.\n981:   bool AnyUnreachableExit;\n982: \n983:   // Whether or not we should iterate on removing dead stores at the end of the\n984:   // function due to removing a store causing a previously captured pointer to\n985:   // no longer be captured.\n986:   bool ShouldIterateEndOfFunctionDSE;\n987: \n988:   /// Dead instructions to be removed at the end of DSE.\n989:   SmallVector<Instruction *> ToRemove;\n990: \n991:   // Class contains self-reference, make sure it's not copied/moved.\n992:   DSEState(Function &F, AliasAnalysis &AA, MemorySSA &MSSA, DominatorTree &DT,\n993:            PostDominatorTree &PDT, const TargetLibraryInfo &TLI,\n994:            const LoopInfo &LI);\n995:   DSEState(const DSEState &) = delete;\n996:   DSEState &operator=(const DSEState &) = delete;\n997: \n998:   LocationSize strengthenLocationSize(const Instruction *I,\n999:                                       LocationSize Size) const;\n1000: \n1001: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.cpp%3FL900-1000"}}}

The `run()` method executes the sequence of passes stored in the pipeline, propagating analysis managers and managing pass state and invalidation.\\n\\n3. **PassBuilderPipelines Implementation** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`): This file contains the complete implementation of `PassBuilder::buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()`, which assembles module and function simplification pipelines. Analyses are registered with `MODULE_ANALYSIS` macros, transformation passes with `MODULE_PASS`, `FUNCTION_PASS`, etc. The PassBuilder includes this file multiple times to extract pass metadata for parsing and instantiation.\\n\\n5. **DeadStoreElimination Concrete Example** (`llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.cpp` and header `llvm/include/llvm/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.h`): The `DSEPass` class (defined in the header) implements the actual dead store elimination optimization.
